class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-148"><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-149" style="margin-left: 0em; margin-right: 0em;">)</span></span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-150" style="vertical-align: 1.54em;"><span class="MJXp-mn" id="MJXp-Span-151">2</span></span></span></span></span></span></span><script type="math/mml" id="MathJax-Element-4"><math display="block" indentalign="left"><mrow><mrow><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><msub><mrow><mi>D</mi></mrow><mrow><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">N</mi></mrow><mrow><msup><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">a</mi></mrow><mrow><mo>+</mo></mrow></msup></mrow></mrow></msub></mstyle></mrow></mrow><mrow><mo linebreak="nobreak">=</mo><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><mfrac><mrow><mn>4</mn></mrow><mrow><mi>π</mi><mi>τ</mi></mrow></mfrac><msup><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo></mrow><mrow><mfrac><mrow><msub><mrow><mi>m</mi></mrow><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">B</mi></mrow></msub><msub><mrow><mi>V</mi></mrow><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">M</mi></mrow></msub></mrow><mrow><msub><mrow><mi>M</mi></mrow><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">B</mi></mrow></msub><mi mathvariant="normal">S</mi></mrow></mfrac></mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mrow><mn>2</mn></mrow></msup><msup><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo></mrow><mrow><mfrac><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">Δ</mi><msub><mrow><mi>E</mi></mrow><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">s</mi></mrow></msub></mrow><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">Δ</mi><msub><mrow><mi>E</mi></mrow><mrow><mi>τ</mi></mrow></msub></mrow></mfrac></mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mrow><mn>2</mn></mrow></msup></mstyle></mrow></math></script></div><div class="label"></div></div>where τ is the pulse duration, <i>m</i><sub>B</sub> is the mass of the active material, <i>V</i><sub>M</sub> is the molar volume, <i>M</i><sub>B</sub> is the molecular weight, <i>S</i> is the interface area, Δ<i>E</i><sub>τ</sub> is the voltage change during the constant current pulse, and Δ<i>E</i><sub>s</sub> is the steady-state voltage change. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref66 ref67 ref68" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref66 ref67 ref68" aria-label="reference 66 to 68">(66−68)</a> The calculated <i>D</i><sub>Na</sub><sup>+</sup> values for NVPF@rGO are in the order magnitude of 10<sup>–10</sup>–10<sup>–11</sup> cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>–1</sup>, higher than those for pure NVPF (10<sup>–11</sup>–10<sup>–12</sup> cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>–1</sup>), revealing a faster Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion behavior in the presence of rGO. Furthermore, NVPF@rGO delivers smaller resistance values compared to NVPF from EIS profiles in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c01894/suppl_file/am4c01894_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S18 and Table S4</a>. These results indicate that the accession of rGO can augment the electronic conductivity, facilitate the Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion speed, and abbreviate the Na<sup>+</sup> transmission path, thereby boosting the cycling and rate capability of NVPF@rGO.</div><div class="NLM_p">To explore the Na<sup>+</sup> insertion/extraction mechanism in the NVPF/rGO electrode, in situ XRD was implemented in the angle ranges of 10–40° during the first cycle displayed in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figures 5</a>a and <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c01894/suppl_file/am4c01894_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">S23</a>. It can be pointed out that the peaks at 38.5° and 39.0° are attributed to the Al mesh (PDF 01-1176) and Al<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> caused by partial oxidation of Al, respectively, which is used as the current collector. The peak at around 18.3° is indexed to the polytetrafluoroethylene (PTFE) binder. The peaks centered at 16.7°, 28.6°, and 33.0° correspond to the (002), (113), and (222) planes of Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3</sub>. During the charging process, the peak of (002) gradually shifts to lower degrees, while the peaks of (113) and (222) shift to higher degrees. The excursion of these characteristic peaks is ascribed to the removal of Na<sup>+</sup>, producing a NaV<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3</sub> phase. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref69" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref69" aria-label="reference 69">(69)</a> XRD pattern can be returned to the initial state during the subsequent discharging process, demonstrating the reversible electrochemical transformation between the two phases. These results reveal a high reversibility of Na<sup>+</sup> insertion/extraction in Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3</sub>, which guarantees favorable electrochemical performance. (a) In situ XRD patterns of NVPF@rGO and the corresponding galvanostatic charge/discharge curves. (b) XRD patterns at different states. (c) Variation of the lattice parameters and volume of the unit cells.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c01894/asset/images/large/am4c01894_0005.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.4c01894&amp;id=fig5"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">In addition, Rietveld refinements were performed for the original, fully charged, and fully discharged states in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figures 5</a>b,c and <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c01894/suppl_file/am4c01894_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">S24–26</a>. The unit cell parameters of Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3</sub> are determined as follows: <i>a</i> = <i>b</i> = 9.040 Å, <i>c</i> = 10.722 Å (<i>R</i>p = 5.86%, <i>R</i>wp = 9.29%), and the corresponding cell volume of 876.219 Å<sup>3</sup> (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figures 5</a>c and <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c01894/suppl_file/am4c01894_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">S24</a>). When charged to 4.3 V, <i>a</i> and <i>b</i> decrease to 8.788 Å and <i>c</i> increases to 10.971 Å (<i>R</i>p = 5.94%, <i>R</i>wp = 9.42%), and the corresponding cell volume reduces to 847.279 Å<sup>3</sup> (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figures 5</a>c and <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c01894/suppl_file/am4c01894_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">S25</a>). The volume change is as low as 3.3%, indicating an extremely low lattice strain of Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3</sub> during the Na<sup>+</sup> extraction process. When discharged to 2.5 V, <i>a</i> and <i>b</i> increase to 8.991 Å, <i>c</i> reduces to 10.680 Å (<i>R</i>p = 5.09%, <i>R</i>wp = 8.83%), and the cell volume returns to 863.351 Å<sup>3</sup> (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figures 5</a>c and <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c01894/suppl_file/am4c01894_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">S26</a>). The volume change is just 1.5% compared to that of the initial state. It can be inferred that the prepared NVPF@rGO exhibits an ultrastable cycling feature owing to the high reversibility and low strain of the crystal lattice.</div><div class="NLM_p">Encouraged by the preeminent performance of the half battery, the electrochemical property of a full battery comprising NVPF@rGO as a cathode and commercial Cu<sub>2</sub>Se as an anode is also investigated in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 6</a>a. Commercial Cu<sub>2</sub>Se with a cubic phase exhibits an irregular block structure with dimensions ranging from 3 to 10 μm in XRD (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c01894/suppl_file/am4c01894_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S27</a>) and SEM (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c01894/suppl_file/am4c01894_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S28</a>). Cu<sub>2</sub>Se provides an average discharge plateau of about 0.9 V and an initial charge capacity of 262 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 0.2 A g<sup>–1</sup> in a half battery (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c01894/suppl_file/am4c01894_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S29</a>). When the full battery is assembled with an NVPF@rGO cathode, the full battery delivers an initial discharge capacity of 116 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>, an initial Coulombic efficiency of 94.7%, and an average discharge voltage of about 2.2 V at 0.2 A g<sup>–1</sup> in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 6</a>b. After the activation process, the capacity is remained at 126 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> after 60 cycles (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 6</a>c). The full battery also exhibits capacities of 125, 134, 132, 129, 122, and 101 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 0.1, 0.2, 0.5, 1, 2, and 5 A g<sup>–1</sup> in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 6</a>d. Once the rate returns to 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup>, the capacity can be restored to 134 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>, revealing a good rate capability. Moreover, the capacity is maintained at 103 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> after 1300 cycles at a high current density of 1 A g<sup>–1</sup> as shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 6</a>e. The exceptional cycling stability and rate performance of NVPF@rGO make it have the potential for application in commercial SIBs.</div><figure id="fig6" data-index="6" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 6</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c01894/asset/images/medium/am4c01894_0006.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c01894/asset/images/large/am4c01894_0006.jpeg" id="gr8" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 6. Electrochemical property of Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3</sub>@rGO//Cu<sub>2</sub>Se full batteries. (a) Schematic illustration of this full battery. (b) Charge/discharge curves of the full battery at 0.2 A g<sup>–1</sup>. (c) Cycling performance at 0.2 A g<sup>–1</sup>. (d) Rate performance. (e) Cycling performance at 1 A g<sup>–1</sup>.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c01894/asset/images/large/am4c01894_0006.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.4c01894&amp;id=fig6"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure></div><div id="sec4" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i11">4.  Conclusions</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p last">In conclusion, NVPF@rGO has been resoundingly synthesized by a microwave-assisted hydrothermal approach with a subsequent calcination treatment. Optimizing the experimental conditions, NVPF@rGO consists of regular NVPF nanocuboids with sizes of 50–150 nm, evenly dispersing on the rGO sheets. When employed as a cathode for SIBs, a high reversible capacity of 123 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> with an initial Coulombic efficiency of 84% at 1 C can be obtained. NVPF@rGO also delivers a capacity of 116 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at the ultrahigh current rate of 50 C. At a high rate of 10 C, a stable capacity of 107 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> with a high conservation ratio of 85.6% can be achieved after 7000 cycles. Moreover, the NVPF@rGO//Cu<sub>2</sub>Se full battery reveals favorable properties. The presence of rGO contributes to enhanced Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion behavior, reduced resistance, and increased pseudocapacitance in NVPF@rGO, leading to preeminent electrochemical properties. The ultrastable rate and cycling performance are also attributed to small lattice change and high structural reversibility during the electrochemical process verified by in situ XRD. Hence, NVPF@rGO is a hopeful cathode material with high voltage, high rate, and ultralong longevity for fast-charging SIBs.</div></div><div class="NLM_back"><div class="article_supporting-info" id="notes1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i12">Supporting Information</h2><div         </div><div class="casAbstract">Na3(VO0.5)2(PO4)2F2 nanoparticles embedded in porous graphene were reported as a superior high-rate cathode material for sodium-ion batteries, exhibiting an excellent electrochem. performance with a high reversible capacity of 100 mA h g-1 at 1 C, 77 mA h g-1 at 50 C, and a capacity retention of 73% after 1000 cycles at 50 C.  In particular, a significant contribution of the pseudocapacitive effect to the Na-storage capacity has been found for the first time.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref2" class="refNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit2" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201700087"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jin, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiao, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrospun NaVPO<sub>4</sub>F/C Nanofibers as Self-Standing Cathode Material for Ultralong Cycle Life Na-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv. Energy Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>7</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1700087</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/aenm.201700087</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D7%26publication_year%3D2017%26pages%3D1700087%26journal%3DAdv.%2BEnergy%2BMater.%26author%3DT.%2BJin%26author%3DY.%2BLiu%26author%3DY.%2BLi%26author%3DK.%2BCao%26author%3DX.%2BWang%26author%3DL.%2BJiao%26title%3DElectrospun%2BNaVPO4F%252FC%2BNanofibers%2Bas%2BSelf-Standing%2BCathode%2BMaterial%2Bfor%2BUltralong%2BCycle%2BLife%2BNa-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1002%252Faenm.201700087&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c01894&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Faenm.201700087&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord empty" id="

                        cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Dendrite-free and long-life Na metal anode achieved by 3D porous Cu</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sun, Jianchao; Guo, Cuiping; Cai, Yajun; Li, Jingjing; Sun, Xueqin; Shi, Weijie; Ai, Shiyun; Chen, Chengcheng; Jiang, Fuyi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">309</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">18-24</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ELCAAV</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4686</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Metallic sodium is an ideal anode for high energy batteries because of its low cost, high natural abundance and suitable redox potential.  However, the practical application of Na metal in rechargeable Na batteries is seriously limited by uneven Na plating and stripping process during cycling, which leads to Na dendrite formation and low Coulombic efficiencies (CEs).  Here, we report that three-dimensional (3D) porous Cu can significantly promote the stability of Na plating/stripping, which features high CEs of 99.4% after 400 cycles at 1 mA cm-2 and low voltage hysteresis voltage (20 mV).  Moreover, 3D porous structure provides highly stable and efficient plating/stripping of Na metal up to 6 mA cm-2.  The excellent performance can be attributed to large sp. surface area of 3D porous Cu and its good wettability of electrolyte, which is beneficial to actual c.d. redn. and non-dendritic growth.  Due to the superior performance of anode, the full battery coupled with Na3V2(PO4)3 cathode exhibited excellent performance that demonstrates its feasibility in practical applications.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref5" class="refNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit5" data-doi="10.1016/j.mtphys.2021.100593"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shao, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guan, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shi, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cai, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tarasenko, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A low-cost NiSe<sub>2</sub> derived from waste nickel foam as a high-performance anode for sodium ion batteries</span>. <i>Mater.                         cas_cit5R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">5</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A low-cost NiSe2 derived from waste nickel foam as a high-performance anode for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yu, Lu; Shao, Lianyi; Wang, Shige; Guan, Jieduo; Shi, Xiaoyan; Cai, Junjie; Tarasenko, Nikolai; Sun, Zhipeng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Materials Today Physics</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">22</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">MTPAD5</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Nickel selenide has a splendid future to become a hot anode for sodium ion batteries owing to the high theor. capacity and unique elec. cond.  Nevertheless, exploring low cost and high-performance nickel selenide is still crit. to further application.  Herein, NiSe2 with micro-structured features has been synthesized through a low-cost and one-step selenidation approach using disused nickel foam as raw material.  Eminent reversible capacity (515 mAh g-1 at 0.1 A g-1), superior rate capability (310 mAh g-1 at 10 A g-1), and excellent cycling stability (318 mAh g-1 after 800 cycles at 1 A g-1) are exhibited for NiSe2 prepd. at 550 °C for 4 h.  Importantly, the initial Coulombic efficiency is also impressive (96%).  Furthermore, the electrochem. mechanism is sufficiently explored by means of ex situ X-ray diffraction (XRD) and transmission electron microscopy (TEM).  Besides, employing Na3V2(PO4)2F3@rGO as cathode and NiSe2 as anode has been assembled the sodium ion full battery, which delivers two high discharge plateaus of 1.86 and 2.72 V and reveals preeminent rate capacity and cycling stability.  This work will come out with a new avenue for fostering the evolution of new metal selenide materials for energy storage and others.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref6" class="refNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit6" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201702619"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qian, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ai, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Prussian Blue Cathode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries and Other Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.         </div><div class="casAbstract">3D ultra-thin carbon networks are ideal skeleton structures for loading active materials as energy storage and conversion devices.  In this work, excellent cathode materials for sodium ion batteries were successfully prepd. by homogeneously anchoring NaxKyMnFe(CN)6 (x + y ≤ 2, NaK-MnHCF) on hierarchical porous 3D N-doped ultra-thin carbon networks (3DNC).         </div><div class="casAbstract">Ion doping strategy is employed to improve the rate performance of insulated Na3V2(PO4)2F3 (NVPF) as cathode of sodium ion batteries.  The concepts of VSU-doping (the valence state of the doping ion keeps unchanged during the synthesis) and VSC-doping (the valence state changes during the synthesis) have been introduced in this research.  Titanium with different valence states (Ti2+, Ti3+, Ti4+) is selected as the doping element to investigate the VSU-doping and VSC-doping effects on NVPF for the first time.  Based on a series of characterizations, it is verified that a moderate Ti doping is able to effectively improve the rate performance of NVPF through the enhancing of electron conduction and sodium ion diffusion, and the advantage is more obvious for the VSC-doping samples.  Among all the NVPF-Tix+0.1 (x = 2, 3, 4) samples, the NVPF-Ti2+0.1 treated with a VSC-doping (Ti source: TiO) possesses the min. particle size distribution (∼40 nm), exhibits the highest initial specific capacity of 125 mA h g-1 at 0.2 C, and a very high rate capability (104 mA h g-1 at 40 C, 81 mA h g-1 at 80 C, 41 mA h g-1 at 200 C) as well, which has surpassed most of the reported results.  When coupling with Na3V2(PO4)3 (NVP) as the anode, the NVPF-Ti2+0.1-NVP pseudo-sym. full cell shows a high initial specific capacity of 99.6 mA h g-1 at 0.2 C and an outstanding rate capability (60% of initial specific capacity at 40 C).  Subsequently, a detailed investigation on the effects of the VSU-doping and VSC-doping processes on the battery performance, in combination with DFT calcns. and anal. of kinetic properties, has been conducted, esp. from the perspective of electron conduction and sodium ion diffusion.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref10" class="refNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit10" data-doi="10.1039/c5cc02251g"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Peia, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High-performance sodium batteries with the 9,10-anthraquinone/CMK-3 cathode and an ether-based electrolyte</span>. <i>Chem.                         cas_cit14R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">14</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Structural evolution of high energy density V3+/V4+ mixed valent Na3V2O2x(PO4)2F3-2x (x = 0.8) sodium vanadium fluorophosphate using in situ synchrotron X-ray powder diffraction</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Serras, Paula; Palomares, Veronica; Rojo, Teofilo; Brand, Helen E. A.; Sharma, Neeraj</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">21</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">7766-7779</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries have become good candidates for energy storage technol.  For this purpose it is crucial to search for and optimize new electrode and electrolyte materials.  Na V fluorophosphates are considered promising cathodes but further studies are required to elucidate their electrochem. and structural behavior.  Therefore, this work focuses on the time-resolved in situ synchrotron x-ray powder diffraction study of Na3V2O2x(PO4)2F3-2x (x = 0.8) while electrochem. cycling.  Reaction mechanism evolution, lattice parameters and Na evolution, and the max. possible Na extn. under the applied electrochem. constraints, are some of the features that were detd. for both a fresh and an offline pre-cycled cell.  The reaction mechanism evolution undergoes a solid soln. reaction with a two-phase region for the 1st lower-potential plateau while a predominantly solid soln. behavior is obsd. for the 2nd higher-potential plateau.  Lattice and vol. evolution is clearly dependent on the Na insertion/extn. mechanism, the Na occupancy and distribution amongst the two crystallog. sites, and the electrochem. cycling history.  The comparison between the fresh and the pre-cycled cell shows that there is a Na site preference depending on the cell and history and that Na swaps from one site to the other during cycling.  This suggests Na site occupancy and mobility in the tunnels is interchangeable and fluid, a favorable characteristic for a cathode in a Na-ion battery.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref15" class="refNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit15" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.202209482"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, J.-Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, H.-X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gu, Z.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Du, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lü, H.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, X.-X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, J. -L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, W.-H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zou, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, X.-L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Heterogeneous NASICON-Type Composite as Low-Cost, High-Performance Cathode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Heterogeneous NASICON-Type Composite as Low-Cost, High-Performance Cathode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Guo, Jin-Zhi; Zhang, Hong-Xia; Gu, Zhen-Yi; Du, Miao; Lue, Hong-Yan; Zhao, Xin-Xin; Yang, Jia-Lin; Li, Wen-Hao; Kang, Shuwen; Zou, Weimin; Wu, Xing-Long</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">32</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">52</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2209482</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1616-301X</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">As promising cathode for sodium-ion batteries, Na+ Superionic Conductor (NASICON)-type materials have attracted attention owing to their excellent structural stability, superior ionic cond., and small vol. expansion.  However, the vanadium-based NASICON-type cathode with the biotoxicity and exorbitant price of V element and the iron-based cathode with low mean working voltage as well as the intrinsic poor electronic cond. of polyanionic compds. hinder their practical applications.  Herein, a double-carbon-layer decorated heterogeneous composite, Na3V2(PO4)3-Na3Fe2(PO4)(P2O7) (NVFPP/C/G), is successfully prepd. for addressing these limitations.  Due to their synergistic effect, NVFPP/C/G exhibits excellent electrochem. performance in half-cell system and superior full-cell performance when matched with hard carbon anode.  Furthermore, the phase compn., electrode kinetics, and phase transition are confirmed by combined analyses of slow scanning power X-ray diffraction, high-resoln. transmission electron microscopy, cyclic voltammetry with various scan rates, galvanostatic intermittent titrn. technique, ex situ X-ray photoelectron spectra, and in situ X-ray diffraction.  This study portends a promising strategy to utilize composite structure engineering for developing advanced polyanionic cathodes.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref16" class="refNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit16" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.2c09122"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ruan, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Du, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">From Solid-Solution MXene to Cr-Substituted Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>: Breaking the Symmetry of Sodium Ions for High-Voltage and Ultrahigh-Rate Cathode Performance</span>. <i>ACS Nano</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>16</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">12</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">21174</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">21185</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit16R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">16</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">From Solid-Solution MXene to Cr-Substituted Na3V2(PO4)3: Breaking the Symmetry of Sodium Ions for High-Voltage and Ultrahigh-Rate Cathode Performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yu, Hong; Ruan, Xiaopeng; Wang, Jinjin; Gu, Zhenyi; Liang, Qinghua; Cao, Jun-Ming; Kang, Jinzhao; Du, Cheng-Feng; Wu, Xing-Long</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">16</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">21174-21185</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Stabilizing Na+ accessibility at high voltage and accelerating Na+ diffusivity are pressing issues to further enhance the energy d. of the Na3V2(PO4)3 (NVP) cathode for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  Herein, by taking a V/Cr solid-soln. MXene as a precursor, a facile in-situ reactive transformation strategy to embed Cr-substituted NVP (NVCP) nanocrystals in a dual-carbon network is proposed.  Particularly, the substituted Cr atom triggers the accessibility of addnl. Na+ in NVCP, which is demonstrated by an addnl. reversible redox plateau at 4.0 V even under extreme conditions.  More importantly, the Cr atom alters the Na+ ordering at the Na2 sites with an addnl. intermediate phase formation during charging/discharging, thus reducing the energy barriers for Na+ migration.  As a result, Na+ diffusivity in NVCP accelerates to 2-3 orders of magnitude higher than that of NVP.  Eventually, the NVCP cathode exhibits extraordinarily high-rate capability (78 mA g-1 at 200 C and 68975 W kg-1), outstanding cycle stability (over 1500 cycles at 10 C), excellent low-temp. property, and full cell performance.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref17"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref17" class="refNumLink">17</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit17" data-doi="10.1007/s12274-022-4687-6"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Heng, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, B.</span></span><span class="NLM_etal"></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Nano self-assembly of fluorophosphate cathode induced by surface energy evolution towards high-rate and stable sodium-ion batteries</span>. <i>Nano Res.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>16</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">1</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">439</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">448</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nano self-assembly of fluorophosphate cathode induced by surface energy evolution towards high-rate and stable sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Gu, Zhen-Yi; Heng, Yong-Li; Guo, Jin-Zhi; Cao, Jun-Ming; Wang, Xiao-Tong; Zhao, Xin-Xin; Sun, Zhong-Hui; Zheng, Shuo-Hang; Liang, Hao-Jie; Li, Bo; Wu, Xing-Long</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Research</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">In the field of materials science and engineering, controlling over shape and crystal orientation remains a tremendous challenge.  Herein, we realize a nano self-assembly morphol. adjustment of Na3V2(PO4)2F3 (NVPF) material, based on surface energy evolution by partially replacing V3+ with aliovalent Mn2+.  Crystal growth direction and surface energy evolution, main factors in inducing the nano self-assembly of NVPF with different shapes and sizes, are revealed by high-resoln. transmission electron microscope combined with d. functional theory.  Furthermore, NVPF with a two-dimensional nanosheet structure (NVPF-NS) exhibits the best rate capability with 68 mAh·g-1 of specific capacity at an ultrahigh rate of 20 C and cycle stability with 80.7% of capacity retention over 1,000 cycles at 1 C.  More significantly, when matched with Se@reduced graphene oxide (rGO) anode, NVPF-NS//Se@rGO sodium-ion full cells display a remarkable long-term stability with a high capacity retention of 93.8% after 500 cycles at 0.5 C and -25 °C.  Consequently, exptl. and theor. calcn. results manifest that NVPF-NS demonstrates such superior performances, which can be mainly due to its inherent crystal structure and preferential orientation growth of {001} facets.  This work will promise insights into developing novel architectural design strategies for high-performance cathode materials in advanced sodium-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref18" class="refNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit18" data-doi="10.1016/j.esci.2021.12.008"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Advanced characterizations and measurements for sodium-ion batteries with NASICON-type cathode materials</span>. <i>eScience</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>2</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">1</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">10</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">31</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit22R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">22</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Core/Double-Shell Structured Na3V2(PO4)2F3@C Nanocomposite as the High Power and Long Lifespan Cathode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Qiang; Meng, Xing; Wei, Zhixuan; Wang, Dongxue; Gao, Yu; Wei, Yingjin; Du, Fei; Chen, Gang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">46</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">31709-31715</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">NASICON-structured Na3V2(PO4)2F3 is considered as a potentially high-capacity cathode material for Na-ion batteries; however, its poor rate capability and insufficient cyclability remain a challenge for battery applications.  To address this issue, we designed and synthesized a core/double-shell structured Na3V2(PO4)2F3@C nanocomposite (Na3V2(PO4)2F3@CD) by in situ C coating and embedding the Na3V2(PO4)2F3 nanoparticles in ordered mesoporous C framework.  Benefiting from the sufficient electrochem. available interfaces and abundant electronic/ionic pathways, this Na3V2(PO4)2F3@CD material demonstrated superior Na+-storage performance with a high reversible capacity of 120 mAh/g at a moderate current of 1 C, a strong high-rate capability with 63 mAh/g at an extremely high rate of 100 C, and a long-cycle lifespan with 65% capacity retention over 5000 cycles.  These superior electrochem. performances remained stable when the Na3V2(PO4)2F3@CD cathode was used in a full cell, suggesting a promising application of the material for high rate and long lifespan Na-ion batteries.  The architectural design and synthetic method developed in this work may provide a new avenue to create high performance Na+-host materials for a wide range of elec. energy storage applications.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref23"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref23" class="refNumLink">23</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit23" data-doi="10.1002/smll.202207148"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guan, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shao, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shi, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Polyanion-Type Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3</sub>@rGO with High-Voltage and Ultralong-Life for Aqueous Zinc Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Small</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>19</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">2207148</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

Today</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>66</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">221</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">244</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.mattod.2023.03.020</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D66%26publication_year%3D2023%26pages%3D221-244%26journal%3DMater.%2BToday%26author%3DJ.%2BGuo%26author%3DZ.%2BGu%26author%3DM.%2BDu%26author%3DX.%2BZhao%26author%3DX.%2BWang%26author%3DX.%2BWu%26title%3DEmerging%2Bcharacterization%2Btechniques%2Bfor%2Bdelving%2Bpolyanion-type%2Bcathode%2Bmaterials%2Bof%2Bsodium-ion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.mattod.2023.03.020&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c01894&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.mattod.2023.03.020&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Emerging characterization techniques for delving polyanion-type cathode materials of sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Guo, Jin-Zhi; Gu, Zhen-Yi; Du, Miao; Zhao, Xin-Xin; Wang, Xiao-Tong; Wu, Xing-Long</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Materials Today (Oxford, United Kingdom)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">66</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">221-244</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">MTOUAN</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1369-7021</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Polyanion-type cathode materials have grown in leaps and bounds and become one of the promising candidates for metal-ion batteries since the successful case of LiFePO4 in lithium-ion batteries, which own stable crystal structure, high thermal stability, good ionic cond., adjustable voltage and chem. compn.  However, further exploration is requisite, such as, the change of crystal/electronic structure, reaction mechanism, and structure evolution during charge/discharge processes, which results from variety of crystal types and redox centers, anion and cationic doping/substitution, as well as transition metal ion migration in polyanion-type materials.  In this review, we focus on the advanced characterization techniques referred in polyanion-type cathode materials of sodium-ion batteries, mainly consist of the structure-related, morphol.-related, compn.-related techniques and in-situ/operando techniques during charge/discharge processes.  The resp. detection mechanisms, scope of application, information available and limitations of each technique are discussed in detail, and the latest developments of these characterization techniques used in polyanion-type materials are summarized.  Advanced characterization techniques play a crucial role in understanding the reaction mechanisms of electrode materials, and can provide an important guiding principle for designing high-performance polyanion-type cathode materials and further optimizing the battery systems of sodium-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref25" class="refNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit25" data-doi="10.1021/acs.chemmater.7b00927"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, C.-C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kopold, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">van Aken, P. A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Maier, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A High Power–High Energy Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3</sub> Sodium Cathode: Investigation of Transport Parameters, Rational Design and Realization</span>. <i>Chem. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>29</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">12</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">5207</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">5215</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acs.chemmater.7b00927</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D29%26publication_year%3D2017%26pages%3D5207-5215%26journal%3DChem.%2BMater.%26issue%3D12%26author%3DC.%2BZhu%26author%3DC.%2BWu%26author%3DC.-C.%2BChen%26author%3DP.%2BKopold%26author%3DP.%2BA.%2Bvan%2BAken%26author%3DJ.%2BMaier%26author%3DY.%2BYu%26title%3DA%2BHigh%2BPower%25E2%2580%2593High%2BEnergy%2BNa3V2%2528PO4%25292F3%2BSodium%2BCathode%253A%2BInvestigation%2Bof%2BTransport%2BParameters%252C%2BRational%2BDesign%2Band%2BRealization%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facs.chemmater.7b00927&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c01894&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facs.chemmater.7b00927&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit25R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">25</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A High Power-High Energy Na3V2(PO4)2F3 Sodium Cathode: Investigation of Transport Parameters, Rational Design and Realization</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhu, Changbao; Wu, Chao; Chen, Chia-Chin; Kopold, Peter; van Aken, Peter A.; Maier, Joachim; Yu, Yan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">29</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5207-5215</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMATEX</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0897-4756</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium ion batteries are realistic and promising alternatives to lithium due to the abundance of Na and the similar intercalation chem. of Na when compared to the lithium counterpart.  Developing high-power and high-energy sodium batteries is still a significant challenge.  Na3V2(PO4)2F3 (NVPF) has been shown to combine excellent charge-discharge kinetics with a competitively high voltage.  However, the major issue is, as for the vast majority of electrode materials, the lack of distinct knowledge of fundamental transport parameters, on which an optimized strategy for developing a high-power and high-energy sodium cathode can be based.  This work aims at filling this gap.  We exptl. investigate the intrinsic ionic and electronic conductivities, as well as the chem. diffusion coeff. of sodium of Na3V2(PO4)2F3 by impedance and dc polarization.  On the basis of these results, we develop an optimized design.  As the electronic cond. is found to be much smaller than the ionic one, electronic wiring of the particles (by a graphene network) has higher priority than providing electrolyte contact.  This is important since the contact by graphene and electrolyte wetting is partly antagonistic, not so much because of interfacial tensions rather because of the introduced heterogeneities on the nanoscale (cf. Lotus effect).  We develop and apply a one-step cost-effective low temp. hydrothermal method without any postheat treatment for the fabrication of a nanoparticulate (∼30-50 nm) NVPF electrode, which provides sufficient porosity and in which every nanoparticle is connected to the graphene network.  In terms of rate capability, the performance of this electrode is excellent and at least belongs to the best Na storage performances reported for Na3V2(PO4)2F3 so far.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref26"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref26" class="refNumLink">26</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit26" data-doi="10.1039/C9TA05396D"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tian, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zou, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Building highly stable and industrial NaVPO<sub>4</sub>F/C as bipolar electrodes for high-rate symmetric rechargeable sodium-ion full batteries</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Synergistically enhanced sodium ion storage from encapsulating highly dispersed cobalt nanodots into N, P, S tri-doped hexapod carbon framework</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu, Shimei; Xu, Feng; Li, Yining; Liu, Chilin; Zhang, Yufei; Fan, Haosen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Colloid and Interface Science</span>

                        cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Mn-Rich Phosphate Cathode for Sodium-Ion Batteries: Anion-Regulated Solid Solution Behavior and Long-Term Cycle Life</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yin, Qi-Min; Gu, Zhen-Yi; Liu, Yan; Lue, Hong-Yan; Liu, Yi-Tong; Liu, Yan-Ning; Su, Meng-Yuan; Guo, Jin-Zhi; Wu, Xing-Long</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">As a sodium superionic conductor, Mn-rich phosphate of Na3.4Mn1.2Ti0.8(PO4)3 is considered as one of the promising cathodes for sodium-ion batteries owing to its good thermodn. stability and high working voltage.  However, Na3.4Mn1.2Ti0.8(PO4)3 is faced with low electronic cond., poor cycling stability and complex phase transition caused by multi-electron transfers, which limits its practical application. Ascribed to unique structure design, the reaction kinetics of Na3.4Mn1.2Ti0.8(PO4)3 are significantly improved, as demonstrated by cyclic voltammetry at varied scan rates and galvanostatic intermittent titrn. technique.  The generated M-F bond inhibits Jahn-Teller effect with an improved cycle stability (85.8 mAh g-1 after 1000 cycles at 5 C with 94.3% capacity retention).  Interestingly, reaction mechanism of Na3.4Mn1.2Ti0.8(PO4)3 with the complex two-phase and solid soln. reactions changes to the whole solid soln. reaction after fluorine substitution, and leads to a smaller vol. change of 5.41% during reaction processes, which is verified by in situ X-ray diffraction.         (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">437</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">141491</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ELCAAV</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na3V2(PO4)2F3 is considered as one of the most promising cathode materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  However, the low electronic cond. of this material severely restricts its electrochem. performance.  Herein, Cr-doped Na3V2(PO4)2F3/C material was synthesized by a simple sol-gel method, and the effects of Cr3+ doping on the structure, morphol. and electrochem. performance were systematically investigated.  The optimized material Na3V2-xCrx(PO4)2F3/C (x = 0.05) exhibits high initial discharge capacity of 101.9 mAh g-1 at 10 C and keep a capacity retention of 68.7 % after 1000 cycles.  The improved electrochem. performance can be attributed to the higher crystallinity, improved intrinsic electronic cond. and sodium ion diffusion coeff. due to the doped Cr3+, which accelerates the electron transport and charge transfer rate.  The optimized Cr-doped Na3V2(PO4)2F3/C material obtained in this work can promote the practical application of Na3V2(PO4)2F3 cathode.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref34" class="refNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit34" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.2c07897"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jia, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Amylopectin-Assisted Fabrication of In Situ Carbon-Coated Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3</sub> Nanosheets for Ultra-Fast Sodium Storage</span>. <i>ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>14</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">36</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">40812</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">40821</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Amylopectin-Assisted Fabrication of In Situ Carbon-Coated Na3V2(PO4)2F3 Nanosheets for Ultra-Fast Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Yue; Song, Wenjun; Tang, Yakun; Jia, Dianzeng; Huang, Yudai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">14</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">36</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">40812-40821</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na3V2(PO4)2F3 is one of the most studied polyanion type cathode materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) and offers great promises.  However, the inferior rate capability induced by its sluggish diffusion of electrons and ions greatly limits the practical application of electrode materials in SIBs.  Herein, we develop an efficient method to fabricate in situ carbon-coated Na3V2(PO4)2F3 nanosheets by using cost-effective amylopectin.  The amylopectin not only could induce the nucleation of Na3V2(PO4)2F3 along its backbone to form a 2D nanostructure, but also act as a source of amorphous carbon for in situ coating on the active material surface.  The composite exhibits extraordinary rate capability (104 mA h g-1 at 40 C, 51 mA h g-1 at 150 C) and desirable cycling stability.  Such satisfactory achievements, esp. the superior rate performance, should be ascribed to its unique 2D nanostructure which shortens the Na+ diffusion length, and the in situ carbon coating endows the composites with effective electron transport.  Even applied to full cells, the obtained devices still display an exceptionally high energy d. (94.8 W h kg-1), high power d. (7295 W kg-1), and excellent cyclic stability.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref35" class="refNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit35" data-doi="10.1002/advs.201800680"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cai, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fang, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pan, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Caging Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3</sub> Microcubes in Cross-Linked Graphene Enabling Ultrafast Sodium Storage and Long-Term Cycling</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Caging Na3V2(PO4)2F3 Microcubes in Cross-Linked Graphene Enabling Ultrafast Sodium Storage and Long-Term Cycling</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cai Yangsheng; Cao Xinxin; Luo Zhigao; Fang Guozhao; Liu Fei; Zhou Jiang; Pan Anqiang; Liang Shuquan; Zhou Jiang; Pan Anqiang; Liang Shuquan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced science (Weinheim, Baden-Wurttemberg, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1800680</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2198-3844</span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries are widely regarded as a promising supplement for lithium-ion battery technology.  However, it still suffers from some challenges, including low energy/power density and unsatisfactory cycling stability.  Here, a cross-linked graphene-caged Na3V2(PO4)2F3 microcubes (NVPF@rGO) composite via a one-pot hydrothermal strategy followed by freeze drying and heat treatment is reported.  As a cathode for a sodium-ion half-cell, the NVPF@rGO delivers excellent cycling stability and rate capability, as well as good low temperature adaptability.  The structural evolution during the repeated Na(+) extraction/insertion and Na ions diffusion kinetics in the NVPF@rGO electrode are investigated.  Importantly, a practicable sodium-ion full-cell is constructed using a NVPF@rGO cathode and a N-doped carbon anode, which delivers outstanding cycling stability (95.1% capacity retention over 400 cycles at 10 C), as well as an exceptionally high energy density (291 Wh kg(-1) at power density of 192 W kg(-1)).  Such micro-/nanoscale design and engineering strategies, as well as deeper understanding of the ion diffusion kinetics, may also be used to explore other micro-/nanostructure materials to boost the performance of energy storage devices.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref36" class="refNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit36" data-doi="10.1039/D2CC04431E"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiao, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shi, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hong, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cai, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shao, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">VO<sub>2</sub>·0.26H<sub>2</sub>O Nanobelts@Reduced Graphene Oxides as Cathode Materials for High-Performance Aqueous Zinc Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Chem.                         cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Comparative study on microwave and conventional hydrothermal pretreatment of bamboo sawdust: Hydrochar properties and its pyrolysis behaviors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Dai, Leilei; He, Chao; Wang, Yunpu; Liu, Yuhuan; Yu, Zhenting; Zhou, Yue; Fan, Liangliang; Duan, Dengle; Ruan, Roger</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy Conversion and Management</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">146</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1-7</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ECMADL</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0196-8904</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Comparative study on microwave and conventional hydrothermal pretreatment of bamboo sawdust was carried out in this study.  Microwave and conventional hydrothermal pretreatment both improved the hydrochar properties and its pyrolysis behaviors.  Proximate and elemental analyses show that the properties of hydrochar from microwave hydrothermal pretreatment are better than conventional hydrothermal pretreatment in terms of calorific value and oxygen content except for 150°C.  Microwave hydrothermal pretreatment removes more acetyl groups in hemicellulose compared to conventional hydrothermal pretreatment, which may be attributed to the hot spot effect of microwave irradn.  The peaks of thermogravimetric and deriv. thermogravimetric curves of pretreated samples always shifted to higher temp. region.  Also, the conventional hydrothermal pretreated samples are more thermally stable than those by microwave heating.  In addn., the glucopyranose content in pyrolysis vapors of microwave hydrothermal pretreated bamboo sawdust (190°C) was 9.82% higher than that from conventional hydrothermal pretreated bamboo sawdust.  However, the acids content from microwave hydrothermal pretreated bamboo sawdust (150°C) was 4.12% lower.  In this regard, microwave hydrothermal pretreatment is more suitable for upgrading the pyrolysis oil quality than conventional hydrothermal pretreatment.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref39" class="refNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit39" data-doi="10.1016/j.scriptamat.2020.02.023"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chu, W.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Microwave-assisted synthesis of porous nano-sized Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3</sub>@C nanospheres for sodium ion batteries with enhanced stability</span>. <i>Scr.                         cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Microwave-assisted synthesis of porous nano-sized Na3V2(PO4)2F3@C nanospheres for sodium ion batteries with enhanced stability</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Mao, Yujia; Zhang, Xiong; Zhou, Yanping; Chu, Wei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Scripta Materialia</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na3V2(PO4)2F3 is a prospective cathode material for sodium ion batteries (SIBs) because of its high theor. capacity.  Nevertheless, its low electronic cond. leads to poor cycling and rate performance, hindering its practical application.  In this work, ultrafine-Na3V2(PO4)2F3 nanocrystals less than 20 nm embedded in porous carbon nanospheres are fabricated via a microwave-assisted glycerol-mediated hydrothermal process followed by annealing.  Microwave irradn. is shown to be crit. for the formation of homogenous ultrafine nanostructure.  The product exhibits a charge/discharge capacity of 106 mAh g-1 at 0.5 C after 100 cycles with a retention of approx. 100% as cathode material for SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref40" class="refNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit40" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.1c21271"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tao, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Manipulating the Phase Compositions of Na<sub>3</sub>(VO<sub>1–x</sub>PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>1+2x</sub> (0 ≤ <i>x</i> ≤ 1) and Their Synergistic Effects with Reduced Graphene Oxide toward High-Rate Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ACS Appl.                         cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Microwave-assisted hydrothermal synthesis, structure and electrochemical properties of the Na3V2-yFeyO2x(PO4)2F3-2x electrode materials for Na-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Shakhova, Iaroslava; Rozova, Marina G.; Burova, Daria; Filimonov, Dmitry S.; Drozhzhin, Oleg A.; Abakumov, Artem M.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Solid State Chemistry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">281</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The Na3V2-yFeyO2x(PO4)2F3-2x (x = 1 - 0.8, y = 0 - 0.8) solid solns. were prepd. using a microwave-assisted hydrothermal technique.  The materials crystallize in the disordered I4/mmm crystal structure as evidenced with electron diffraction and Rietveld refinement from powder x-ray diffraction data (Na3V1.2Fe0.8O1.6(PO4)2F1.4: a 6.38666(9), c 10.6562(2) Å, R = 0.023, RP = 0.013).  A combination of EELS and 57Fe Mossbauer spectroscopy revealed that V is in the mixed 4+/5+ oxidn. state, whereas Fe is exclusively in the 3+ state, thus pointing to the V4+ → Fe3+/V5+ co-substitution.  The solid solns. demonstrate reversible Na+ (de)intercalation in the electrochem. cells with Na metal counter-electrode through two sloping potential plateaus at ∼3.5 and 4.0 V vs. Na+/Na.  The electrochem. capacity decays from 105 mAh/g for y = 0 to ∼50 mAh/g for y = 0.8 because of decreasing amt. of electrochem. active V4+ upon increasing the Fe content.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref42"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref42" class="refNumLink">42</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit42" data-doi="10.1039/D2TA00565D"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qin, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ding, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Structure, composition and electrochemical performance analysis of fluorophosphates from different synthetic methods: is really Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3</sub> synthesized?</span>. <i>J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">In this article, Na3V2(PO4)3/carbon nanocomposites with different carbon contents were prepd. by a one-step solid state reaction and evaluated in different electrolyte systems.                         cas_cit47R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">47</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Synthesis of uniform hierarchical Na3V1.95Mn0.05(PO4)2F3@C hollow microspheres as a cathode material for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Yu; Guo, Shirui; Xu, Huayun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Uniform hierarchical Na3V1.95Mn0.05(PO4)2F3@C hollow microspheres composed of nanoplates and nanoparticles were synthesized by a 1-step polyol-assisted hydrothermal method combined with chem. vapor deposition (CVD).  We also studied the formation mechanism of the hierarchical hollow microspheres and it was found that both tetraethylene glycol and citric acid play important roles in the formation of the hierarchical hollow microspheres.  Na3V1.95Mn0.05(PO4)2F3@C showed an initial reversible capacity of 122.9 mAh/g and the discharge capacity of 109 mAh/g was maintained with a coulombic efficiency of 99.1% after 500 cycles.  The unique architecture, enhanced electronic cond. and improved diffusion coeff. of Na ions for Na3V2(PO4)2F3 by Mn2+ doping as well as C coating account for the enhanced electrochem. properties.  Therefore, we present an approach to design a tunable structure for multi-element compds. with enhanced electrochem. performance as a promising cathode material for practical applications.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref48"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref48" class="refNumLink">48</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit48" data-doi="10.1021/acs.nanolett.7b00889"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tao, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Archer, L.                         cas_cit48R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">48</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-Capacity and Ultrafast Na-Ion Storage of a Self-Supported 3D Porous Antimony Persulfide-Graphene Foam Architecture</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lu, Yanying; Zhang, Ning; Jiang, Shuang; Zhang, Yudong; Zhou, Meng; Tao, Zhanliang; Archer, Lynden A.; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">17</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3668-3674</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NALEFD</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1530-6984</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The key challenge for high-performance sodium-ion batteries is the exploitation of appropriate electrode materials with a long cycling stability and high rate capability.  Here, we report Sb2S5 nanoparticles (∼5 nm) uniformly encapsulated in three-dimensional (3D) porous graphene foam, which were fabricated by a facile hydrothermal coassembly strategy, as a high-performance anode material for sodium-ion batteries.  The as-prepd. composite can be directly used as electrodes without adding a binder or current collector, exhibiting outstanding electrochem. performance with a high reversible capacity (845 mA h g-1 at 0.1 A g-1), ultralong cycling life (91.6% capacity retention after 300 cycles at 0.2 A g-1), and exceptional rate capability (525 mA h g-1 at 10.0 A g-1).  This is attributed to fast Na+ ion diffusion from the ultrasmall nanoparticles and excellent elec. transport between the active material and 3D porous graphene, which also provide an effective strategy for anchoring the nanoparticles.  Exptl. results show that the Sb2S5 undergoes a reversible reaction of Sb2S5 + 16Na &lt;-&gt;tmr 5Na2S + 2Na3Sb during sodiation/desodiation.  Moreover, a full cell with Na3(VO0.5)2(PO4)2F2/C cathode and the as-prepd. composite anode was assembled, displaying high output voltage (∼2.2 V) with a stable capacity of 828 mA h g-1 for anode material (with 100 cycles at 0.1 A g-1), showing the potential for practical application.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref49"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref49" class="refNumLink">49</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit49" data-doi="10.1016/j.scib.2020.01.018"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Carbon-coating-increased working voltage and energy density towards an advanced Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3</sub>@C cathode in sodium-ion batteries</span>. <i>Sci.
